      "text": "The conflict between high reconstruction costs and low accuracy inlarge-scale scene reconstruction,drivenby scene complexity,remainsakeychallengein3Dreconstruction.RecentNeRFvariants using heuristic partitioning [38,39,44] or voxel grids [2,6,26,45] have supported performance in large-scale scenes but are limited by long training times.Alternatively, 3D Gaussian Splatting (3DGS) has introduced methods like progressive [14, 17, 49] and level-of-detail (LOD) schemes [21, 30] to balance quality and efficiency. ## EGGS: Expert-Guided Framework Constructed from Semantic Priors for Large-Scale Scene Reconstruction

AnonymousCVPRsubmission

Figure1.Comparisonof EGGS(ours)with OctreeGS and CityGSv2.EGGS achieves clearer and morefaithful detail reconstruction across large scene. (Higher PSNR values reflect higher-fidelity reconstruction)

<!-- image -->

## Abstract

| 001 NeuralRadianceFields(NeRF）and3DGaussianSplatting 002 (3DGS)havedemonstratedstrongcapabilityinreconstructing3D 003 scenesrangingfromindoorto outdoorenvironments.Forlarge- 004 scalescenes,reconstructionis often acceleratedthroughparal- 005 lelizationbased ongeographicpartitioning.However,excessive 006 scenesizeintroducesviewpointlocality,leadingtotwomajorchal- 007 lenges:reconstructionisolation andredundantcomputation.The 008 formercausessignificantinconsistencyinrenderingqualityacross 600 viewpointsandthelatterleadstorepetitiveoptimizationofsimilar 010 elements,resulting inwastedcomputational resources.Inspired 011 by theexpert optimization principleinMixture-of-Experts(MoEs), 012 weproposeEGGS(Expert-GuidedFrameworkConstructedfrom 013 SemanticPriorsforLarge-ScaleSceneReconstruction),anexpert- 014 guidedframeworkthatreplacesgeographicpartitioningwithex- 015 pertcollaborationconstructedfromsemanticpriors.EGGSas- 016 signsexpertstosceneelementsbasedonsemanticandfeature 017 similarity,enablingsemantic-awarecollaborationthateffectively   |

alleviatesisolationandredundancy.Extensiveexperimentson bothsyntheticandreal-worlddatasetsdemonstratethatEGGs achievesstate-of-the-artreconstructionquality,outperformingexistingmethodsbyupto5%inPSNR.Codeanddatasetswillbe released upon acceptance.

## 1. Introduction

NeRF [1, 25] and 3DGS [9,13] have demonstrated efficient 3D reconstruction capabilities across diverse scales, ranging from small indoor scenes [22] to large outdoor environments, supporting downstream tasks such as SLAM and AR content creation [37]. Current large-scale reconstruction methods [17, 21, 38, 42, 45] typically adopt geographic region-based parallel algorithms,whereeachsubregionisindependently optimizedtoaccelerate reconstruction.However, these methods fail to address the viewpoint locality problem inherent in large-scale scenes.Unlike indoor settings with near-complete scene capture, each viewpoint

018

033

- 034 in outdoor scenes only observes a partial area,leading to three ma035 jorissues.

036 First,ReconstructionIsolation.Each subregionreconstruc037 tionrelies on theviewpoints that observeitsinternalcontent. 038 Since viewpoints only provide limited coverage within individ039 ualregions,reconstruction qualityvaries significantly across sub040 regions, an issue unique to large-scale reconstruction.Recent 041 042 tional loss constraints, yet viewpoint locality remains unresolved: 043 high-quality subregionsfail toenhance adjacent low-quality ones, 044 ultimatelydegrading overall reconstructionfidelity.

Second,Redundant Computation.Geographic partitioning separates semantic entities such as buildings,vegetation, and roads;duetoviewpointlocality,theseelements arerepeatedly "rediscovered" and "relearned".This scheme overlooks semantic and structuralredundancy,causingrepetitive subregionreconstructions that raise computational costs and reduce overall reconstruction quality.

Third, Multi-Expert Collaboration and Competition. Modular-GS[34] introduce MoEs [31] into 3DGS for semantic space decomposition.Inspired by the expert division strategyin MOEs for 3D reconstruction,we propose that an expert-guided structure can go beyond semantic segmentation and serve as an alternative to geographic partitioning.However, the multi-experts structurenaturallyinvolvesexpert competitionandcooperation, whichnecessitates designingcollaborativemechanismstoprevent boundary ambiguity that could impair rendering quality.

To address these challenges, we present EGGS, an ExpertGuidedFrameworkConstructedfromSemanticPriorsforLargeScale Scene Reconstruction, which replaces geographic partitioningwithasemanticpriormulti-expertguidedframework.EGGS significantlyimprovesreconstructionbalanceacrosslarge-scale scenes and reducing computational cost for higher-quality reconstruction across the whole scene. At its core, EGGS leverages struction through three key parts: First, semantic segmentation divides the scene intomultiple categories,each assigned to a category expert trained with semantically rich viewpoints for corresponding instance learning and reconstruction.Second,category experts further guide the reconstruction of unselected viewpoints, mitigating reconstruction isolation caused by viewpoint locality and achieving balanced,efficientreconstruction.Third,a collaborative and constraint-based mechanism promotes expert cooperation and suppresses inter-expert conflicts, alleviating boundaryinduced blurring.

Extensive experiments in Fig. 6 and Tab. 2 demonstrates that EGGSachievesmorebalanced andefficientreconstructionthan spatial partitioning methods,improving overall reconstruction quality by up to 5% in PSNR.As presented in Fig. 1,EGGS provides more accurate and detailed reconstructions than existing large-scale approaches.Ourmaincontributions aresummarized as follows:

- 1.We propose a novel expert-guided framework for large-scale 3D reconstruction, addressing rendering isolation and redundant computation inherent in geographic partitioning methods. To our best knowledge, this is the first work to apply expert guidanceforlarge-scalereconstruction.
2. We design a complete expert construction and training pipeline
- that effectivelyimprovesreconstruction balance whilereducing overallcomputationalcost.
- 3.We introduce a contribution-weighted expert collaboration algorithm that mitigates boundary ambiguity caused by interexpertcompetition.
- 4.Extensive experiments on both synthetic and real-world datasetsvalidatethatEGGSimprovingoverallreconstruction ficiency.

## 2.Related Work

## 2.1.Large-scaleSceneReconstruction

The conflict between high reconstruction costs and low accuracy inlarge-scale scene reconstruction,drivenby scene complexity,remainsakeychallengein3Dreconstruction.RecentNeRFvariants using heuristic partitioning [38,39,44] or voxel grids [2,6,26,45] have supported performance in large-scale scenes but are limited by long training times.Alternatively, 3D Gaussian Splatting (3DGS) has introduced methods like progressive [14, 17, 49] and level-of-detail (LOD) schemes [21, 30] to balance quality and efficiency. However, these geographically partitioned methods still sufferfrominconsistentreconstructionqualityduetoviewpoint limitations,leading todegraded overall results.

## 2.2.Semantic-awareness

With advancementsin2Dsemanticunderstanding[15,29],recent researchhasexploredsemanticintegrationin3Dreconstruction [3,8,28,47].Some methods embed semantic information into features or aggregating semanticpools[7].Othersleverage external semanticmodels toguide3DGS training orinference[51], such asintroducingsemanticviewpointsconsistencylossestomitigate overfitting [11, 41]. These efforts highlight the potential of semantic-awaremethods in3Dreconstruction[27],yet their applicationin complex,large-scalescenesrequiresfurtherexploration. Inspiredby thegrowingfieldof3Dspatialsemanticawareness, we aimtoleveragerichsemanticinformationinlarge-scalescenes to overcome viewpoint limitations and enable optimization regardless ofspatialdistance.

## 2.3.MoEsandMulti-ExpertFramework

MoEsframework[10,12,35]enablesparalleltrainingthroughexpert specialization. Recent successes in visual imaging [31, 46] have inspired its application in 3D reconstruction.Existing work has combined MoEs with 3D reconstruction[4,5,19,34]and made improvements for large-scale scenes[24,50].However, prior works have largely ignored the role of experts as reusable semanticpriors capableofguidingsimilar objects thatfrequently appear in large-scale scenes.

## 3.1. Overview

EGGS is a large-scale collaborative reconstruction framework based on a semantic partitioned multi-expert model.Instead of dividing scenes into geographic blocks,EGGS establishes a completereconstructionpipeline throughtwomajor systems:an expert-guidedframework and expert collaborativereconstruction. These correspond to three key modules:Semantic-Prior Filtering,ExpertDivision&amp;GuidanceandExpertCollaborativeReconstruction.

The semantic prior filtering module employs a dual filtering mechanismbasedonsemantics andclusteringtoselectviewpoints and corresponding point clouds that are semantically rich and exhibit strong multi-view consistencyfrom large-scale scenes.These selectedviewpoints areprioritized duringreconstruction,producinghigh-qualityGaussian anchorsthatformcategory-specificexpertsrepresenting different semantic classes.

Theexpert-guidedreconstructionmoduletreatstheseexperts as reconstruction priors.During the preliminary reconstruction stage, EGGS performs stable matching between experts and spatially scatteredyet semantically consistent elements across the scene,enabling one-to-one expert guidance. Through a graph neural network, prior knowledge is propagated from experts to guide the reconstruction of these elements,achieving high-quality and balanced results. This design effectively mitigates the reconstrucand"relearned")caused by viewpoint locality and isolated renderingofrepeatedstructures.

Finally,the expert collaboration mechanism addresses the intrinsic competition-cooperation problem introduced by replacing geographic partitioning with a multi-expert framework.By assigning gradient weights based on rendering quality, EGGS promotes expert cooperation during reconstruction.Additionally,an flicts at expert boundaries, alleviating edge blurring and ensuring coherent global reconstruction.

## 3.2.Expert-Guided Framework

## 3.2.1. Semantic-Prior Filtering.

Semantic-priorfilteringmoduleofEGGStakescameraviewpoints,point clouds, and semantic segmentation masks as input to generate a subset of viewpoints and point clouds prioritized for expert reconstruction. This module incorporates a Segmented-Prior filtering mechanism consisting of SegmentedFilter andviewpoint clustering.The semantic segmentation mask prior is obtained using theCLIP+SAM[15,29]modelguidedbytextualprompts to capture semantic regions,as detailed in the supplementary material,including model parameters and settings. Semantic score filteringselects theviewpoints andpoint clouds thatbestrepresent expert-specific reconstruction regions, while viewpoint clustering

Step 1:Segmented Filter.To quantify the scene information richness of all semantic categories within each viewpoint and prioritize viewpoints that capture more structural details for highquality expert reconstruction,we define the semantic score as a measure of thesemanticrichnesscapturedby a singleviewpoint. This score is computed through the interaction between the 3D point cloud constructed via SfM[33] and the semantic masks associatedwitheachviewpoint.

Each3Dpointhasauniqueindexpidjand associated 2Dkeyviewpoints in which thepoint is visible.These coordinatesrepresent theprojectionpositions andvisibilityofeach3Dpoint across viewpoints. For a given viewpoint cam,its semantic score Scam is obtained by intersecting all semantic masks of that viewpoint withitscorrespondingkeypoint coordinates and summing overthe projected counts:

<!-- formula-not-decoded -->

Here,K denotes the set of all semantic categories,k E K represents the k-th semantic subcategory, and Mk is the semantic mask of category k in viewpoint cami.A higher semantic score Scam indicates that the viewpoint contains richer semantic information across all categories,making it more favorable for high-quality reconstruction. Therefore, Scam serves as a crucial criterionfor selectingviewpoints assigned to expert models.

Step 2:Viewpoint Clustering.Relying solely on semantic richness toselectviewpoints andpointcloudsforexpertreconstructionmay compromiseviewpoints consistency,leading to severe viewpoint locality issues. To address this, we introduce an additional viewpoint clustering stage based on theK-Means algorithm, which partitions all viewpoints into multiple clusters accordingtotheircameraparameters.

Within each cluster, viewpoints are ranked by their semantic scores Scam. A threshold hyperparameter Top\_n% is then applied to select the top n%viewpoints and their corresponding point clouds for expert-prior reconstruction. This process ensures that each expert receives semantically rich yet spatially diverse inputs,thereby preserving viewpoints consistency and improving reconstructionbalance acrosslarge-scale scenes.

## 3.2.2.Expert Division &amp; Guidance.

Expert Construction.The reconstructionisolation and redundant computationissuescausedbyviewpointlocalityessentiallystem from the absence of a unified global paradigm to guide and constrainreconstruction across spatially distributed objects.Under limitedviewpoint coverage,identical structures cannotbe consistentlycapturedfromaglobalperspective,resultinginfragmented reconstructions.

Toaddress this,EGGS constructs multiple category-specific experts using the semantically rich viewpoints and correspondingpointcloudsobtainedfromthesemanticpriorfilteringmodule.These selected data are first reconstructed through a priority reconstruction process, generating high-quality Gaussian anchors thatserve asthefoundationofeachexpert.Eachcategoryexpertis composed of Gaussian anchors corresponding toitssemantic category and acts as a global prior to guide consistent reconstruction across the entire scene, as illustrated in Fig. 2.

Stage1:Multi-ScaleStableMatching.The stablematching algorithm connects themulti-categoryexpertsobtainedfrompriorityreconstructionwiththeir correspondingsemanticinstances across the scene, regardless of geographic separation. By establishingassociationspurelybasedonfeaturesimilarityrather than spatial proximity, this process eliminates reconstruction isolation caused byinconsistent reconstruction ofsemanticallyidenticalobjects distributed across large-scale scenes.

Considering thattheclassicalstablematching algorithmhas a computational complexity of O(n²),performingglobalfeature association among all Gaussian anchors is computationally prohibitive. To address this, we propose a multi-scale stable matching schemebased on an Octreehierarchicalstructure,whichreduces the overall time complexity from O(n²)to O(n log n),thus meeting the efficiency requirements of expert-guided reconstruction in large-scale scenarios,as shown inFig.3.

Specifically,for eachsemanticclass,the algorithmiteratively performs stable matching within Octree sub-blocks,pairing Gaussian anchors from category-specific experts with those of scene

Since thedistributions ofoptandunoptanchorswithinOctree sub-blocks are not always uniform,thehierarchical multi-level matching ensures that any unmatched anchors in higherlevels can still be matched inlowerlevels or during global matching,thereby maintainingcompleteness andstability of theexpertguidanceprocess.

## 3.3.ExpertCollaborativeReconstruction

To address boundary ambiguity and collaboration challenges in multi-expert models,EGGS introduces two mechanisms that convertGaussian anchorswith ambiguous attributionintocollaborativebridges acrossexpert domains.

Suppose there are experts corresponding toKsemanticcategories,withthetotallossfunctiondenoted as L. ## 4.Experiment

This sectionpresentstheexperimentalevaluation ofEGGS.Section 4.1 introduces the datasets,baseline algorithms and experimental setup. Section 4.2 compares EGGS with existing methods in terms of renderingquality acrossfive datasets.Section 4.3employs radar charts to demonstrate EGGS's improvements in balancingper-viewrendering quality and alleviating isolation caused by perspective locality. Section 4.4 explores the impact of key hyperparameters and presents ablation studies toevaluate the contribution of each component. Finally, Section 4.5 discusses potential improvements and outlines directions for future work.

## 4.1.Experimental Setup

Dataset Configuration.EGGS is evaluated on five large-scale datasets,including one syntheticurban dataset (MatrixCity[16]), two real-world datasets (Hospital and P1 HuiTian),and two complexscenes(Residence andArtSci)from the open-sourceUrbanScene3D dataset[18].MatrixCity is sampled from the SmallCity dataset,whereas Hospital and P1HuiTian arereal-world datasets collectedfromactualurbanenvironments.

For benchmarking, EGGS is compared against four SOTA large-scalereconstructionmethods:OctreeGS,CityGSv2,GrendelGS,andScaffoldGS.AllexperimentsforEGGS,ScaffoldGS, andGrendelGSareconductedonasingleNvidiaV100GPU,with 30,000 training iterations.Due toits two-stage design,CityGSv2 is trained using 15,000 coarse iterations followed by 15,000 finetuning iterations.

For quantitative evaluation, we adopt PSNR, SSIM[43], and LPIPS[48] to comprehensively assess reconstruction performance. Additionally, to highlight EGGS's effectiveness in addressing viewpoint-localcoverageimbalanceandredundantcomputation,wefurther report the standard deviation(Std）of PSNR across viewpoints as a measure of reconstruction consistency,and the total training time(min)over30,000iterations as anindicator of computational efficiency. For a fair comparison, all models are trained with identical hyperparameter settings, which are detailed in the supplementary material.

## 4.2.Rendering Quality

EGGS achieves superior rendering performance on both the syntheticMatrixCityandreal-worlddatasetsthroughmulti-expert guided optimization. As shown in Tab. 1 and Fig. 4, its overall reconstruction quality matches or surpasses current SOTA methods,with consistentlyhigherPSNRvalues uptoa5%gain on the Hospital dataset.On the Residence dataset,EGGS's SSIM and LPIPS are slightly lower than the best results.We attribute this tothedataset'sdenseresidentiallayout,wherea singleviewpoint alreadycovers abundantscene content,yieldinganaturaleffect similar toEGGS's experts.This observation highlights the importance of viewpoint coverage in large-scale reconstruction and explainsthecloseperformancebetweenEGGSandotherSOTA baselines in this case.For the MatrixCity scene, the relatively low performance of OctreeGS may partially stemfrom conflicts caused by using unified hyperparameter settings across all methods.

## 4.3.PerspectiveBalanceExperiment

The core idea of the EGGS expert guidance framework is toleverage the Gaussian anchors of high-quality category experts to guide theoptimizationof correspondinganchorsinthesamesemantic category, thereby improving the overall reconstruction quality of the entire scene. For large-scale scenes, if the rendering quality across all novelviewpoints is more uniform and maintains high

Toevaluatetheroleofeachmodulein theEGGSalgorithm, we conducted ablation experiments, and the results are shown in Tab.3.Wefirstinvestigatewhether thesemanticsegmentation prior has a significant influence on the final reconstruction quality.To this end,we remove the semantic segmentation module and replace it with a strategy that selects experts based on the information richness between images and point clouds.As shown in theresults,thedifferenceis minor.We attribute this to thefact that semantic segmentation serves as a suggestive classification mechanism for category expert selection, while the final expert guidancerelies onfeature similarity and themulti-scale stable matching algorithm,which dynamicallyreassignsemanticlabels based on high-similarity features.Therefore,possiblemisclassificationsinsemanticsegmentationhavelimited impact onthefinal reconstruction,as the matching process corrects such errors during optimization.

## 4.5.Future andLimitation

twomajor challengesposedbythelocal coverageoflarge-scale scene perspectives.Currently, the evolving 3D spatial semantic segmentation technology[51] seems to be able to replace the original 2D semantic prior, which had limitations in accuracy, providing EGGS with a more outstanding prior enhancement.

## 5. Conclusion

This paper presents EGGS, an expert-guided framework for largescale scene reconstruction.EGGS identifies the viewpoint locality in large-scale scenes, which gives rise to two challenges: reconstruction isolation and redundant computation.By leveraging semantic priors to construct experts and employing an expert-guided reconstructionstrategy,EGGSmitigatesisolation-inducedquality inconsistency and achieves competitivereconstructionefficiency. An expert collaboration mechanismfurther resolves the boundary ambiguityintroduced by experts.Experiments showthat existing methods degrade under viewpoint locality,whereas EGGS maintains balanced cross-viewreconstruction quality and achieves SOTA performance across diverse datasets,withimprovements of up to5% in PSNR.
